           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFMeeks2003" class="citation book cs1">Meeks, Blair Gilmer (2003). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=--Wv5kiq-RoC&amp;q=9780687044542"><i>Season of Ash and Fire: Prayers and Liturgies for Lent and Easter</i></a>. Abingdon Press. p.&nbsp;107. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780687044542" title="Special:BookSources/9780687044542"><bdi>9780687044542</bdi></a>. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20140707003455/http://books.google.com/books?id=--Wv5kiq-RoC&amp;dq=9780687044542&amp;source=gbs_navlinks_s">Archived</a> from the original on 7 July 2014. <q>In recent years Christians from the Reformed branch of the Protestant tradition have begun to recover a practice that dates in the Western church at least to the tenth century. That is to begin Lent on the Wednesday before the First Sunday in Lent with a service of repentance and commitment, including the imposition of ashes. The Lutheran and Anglican traditions, of course, never lapsed in this observance, and the liturgical reforms of Vatican II have made Roman Catholic prayers and rubrics more accessible to other traditions through ecumenical dialogues.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Season+of+Ash+and+Fire%3A+Prayers+and+Liturgies+for+Lent+and+Easter&amp;rft.pages=107&amp;rft.pub=Abingdon+Press&amp;rft.date=2003&amp;rft.isbn=9780687044542&amp;rft.aulast=Meeks&amp;rft.aufirst=Blair+Gilmer&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3D--Wv5kiq-RoC%26q%3D9780687044542&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAsh+Wednesday" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li>

Church Publishing, Inc. 1979. p.&nbsp;265. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780898690613" title="Special:BookSources/9780898690613"><bdi>9780898690613</bdi></a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Book+of+Common+Prayer+and+Administration+of+the+Sacraments+and+Other+Rites+and+Ceremonies+of+the+Church%3A+Together+with+the+Psalter+Or+Psalms+of+David+According+to+the+Use+of+the+Episcopal+Church&amp;rft.pages=265&amp;rft.pub=Church+Publishing%2C+Inc.&amp;rft.date=1979&amp;rft.isbn=9780898690613&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DZTMQAAAAYAAJ%26q%3DThe%2BBook%2Bof%2BCommon%2BPrayer%2Band%2BAdministration%2Bof%2Bthe%2BSacraments%2Band%2BOther%2BRites%2Band%2BCeremonies%2Bof%2Bthe%2BChurch%3A%2BTogether%2Bwith%2Bthe%2BPsalter%2BOr%2BPsalms%2Bof%2BDavid%2BAccording%2Bto%2Bthe%2BUse%2Bof%2Bthe%2BEpiscopal%2BChurch&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAsh+Wednesday" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-Canfield-101"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Canfield_101-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Canfield_101-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFMonte_Canfield2009" class="citation web cs1">Monte Canfield (20 February 2009). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://open.salon.com/blog/monte_canfield/2009/02/20/ash_wednesday_what_is_it_about">"Ash Wednesday: What is it About?"</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Salon_(website)" title="Salon (website)">Salon</a></i>. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20140306024921/http://open.salon.com/blog/monte_canfield/2009/02/20/ash_wednesday_what_is_it_about">Archived</a> from the original on 6 March 2014. <q>After the Reformation most Protestant church denominations, while recognizing Ash Wednesday as a holy day, did not engage in the imposition of ashes. Many Anglican, Episcopal and some Lutheran churches did continue the rite but it was mostly reserved for use in the Roman Catholic Church. During and after the ecumenical era that resulted in the Vatican II proclamations, many of the Protestant denominations encouraged a liturgical revival in their churches and the Ash Wednesday imposition of ashes was encouraged.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Salon&amp;rft.atitle=Ash+Wednesday%3A+What+is+it+About%3F&amp;rft.date=2009-02-20&amp;rft.au=Monte+Canfield&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fopen.salon.com%2Fblog%2Fmonte_canfield%2F2009%2F02%2F20%2Fash_wednesday_what_is_it_about&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAsh+Wednesday" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-KingsburyPennington1980-102"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-KingsburyPennington1980_102-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFKingsburyPennington1980" class="citation book cs1">Kingsbury, Jack D.; Pennington, Chester (1980). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=mi1I4v1KDhEC"><i>Lent</i></a>. Fortress Press. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780800640934" title="Special:BookSources/9780800640934"><bdi>9780800640934</bdi></a>. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20140704192338/http://books.google.com/books?id=mi1I4v1KDhEC">Archived</a> from the original on 4 July 2014. <q>The imposition of ashes symbolizes the penitential nature of the season of Lent. While this custom is still observed in the Roman Catholic church, and in some Lutheran and Anglican parishes, it has not been retained in Reformed churches.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Lent&amp;rft.pub=Fortress+Press&amp;rft.date=1980&amp;rft.isbn=9780800640934&amp;rft.aulast=Kingsbury&amp;rft.aufirst=Jack+D.&amp;rft.au=Pennington%2C+Chester&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3Dmi1I4v1KDhEC&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAsh+Wednesday" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-Anderson1996-103"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Anderson1996_103-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFAnderson1996" class="citation book cs1">Anderson, Russell F. (1996). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=GbHjXgDWZdwC&amp;pg=PA104"><i>Lectionary Preaching Workbook</i></a>. CSS Publishing. p.&nbsp;104. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780788008214" title="Special:BookSources/9780788008214"><bdi>9780788008214</bdi></a>. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20140628191645/http://books.google.com/books?id=GbHjXgDWZdwC&amp;pg=PA104">Archived</a> from the original on 28 June 2014. <q>Ashes are a traditional symbol of penitence and remorse. The practice of imposing ashes on the first day of Lent continues to this day in the church of Rome as well as in many Lutheran and Episcopalian quarters.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Lectionary+Preaching+Workbook&amp;rft.pages=104&amp;rft.pub=CSS+Publishing&amp;rft.date=1996&amp;rft.isbn=9780788008214&amp;rft.aulast=Anderson&amp;rft.aufirst=Russell+F.&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DGbHjXgDWZdwC%26pg%3DPA104&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAsh+Wednesday" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li>

Retrieved <span class="nowrap">8 March</span> 2011</span>. <q>This is the day Lent begins. Christians go to church to pray and have a cross drawn in ashes on their foreheads.          <li id="cite_note-107"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-107">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://archives.umc.org/interior.asp?ptid=16&amp;mid=6710">The United Methodist Church website: "When did United Methodists start the "imposition of ashes" on Ash Wednesday?"</a> retrieved 1 March 2014 | <i>"While many think of actions such as the imposition of ashes, signing with the cross, footwashing, and the use of incense as something that only Roman Catholics or high church Episcopalians do, there has been a move among Protestant churches, including United Methodists to recover these more multisensory ways of worship."</i></span> </li>

         <li id="cite_note-113"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-113">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">

New Liturgical Movement. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20140508014116/http://www.newliturgicalmovement.org/2014/02/septuagesima-in-ambrosian-rite.html#.U5PZQnJdWSo">Archived</a> from the original on 8 May 2014. <q>The Ambrosian Rite still to this day has no Ash Wednesday; it is therefore Quinquagesima that forms the prelude to Lent, properly so-called, which the Roman Rite has in Ash Wednesday and the ferias "post Cineres".</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Septuagesima+in+the+Ambrosian+Rite&amp;rft.pub=New+Liturgical+Movement&amp;rft.date=2014-02-16&amp;rft.aulast=Dipippo&amp;rft.aufirst=Gregory&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.newliturgicalmovement.org%2F2014%2F02%2Fseptuagesima-in-ambrosian-rite.html%23.U5PZQnJdWSo&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAsh+Wednesday" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li>
